# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy Extension Registry and Factory Architecture

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement the extension registry pattern: the Registry template class, the RegisterFactory macro usage, the factory lookup by name, and how extensions self-register at static initialization time.

44-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully created a comprehensive analysis of the Envoy extension registry pattern. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

I've identified all the C++ source files implementing the extension registry pattern in envoyproxy/envoy (v1.31.2):

### Core Architecture Components:

1. **Registry Template Class** (`envoy/registry/registry.h:166-493`)
   - `FactoryRegistry<Base>` maintains a static hash map of factories
   - Provides `getFactory()`, `getFactoryByType()`, and `registerFactory()` methods
   - Supports both name-based and type-based factory lookup

2. **RegisterFactory Template** (`envoy/registry/registry.h:507-597`)
   - Automatically registers factory instances with the registry
   - Works as a CRTP pattern with static instantiation
   - Supports both static and dynamic registration modes

3. **Registration Macros** (`envoy/registry/registry.h:618-665`)
   - `REGISTER_FACTORY()` - Static factory registration
   - `LEGACY_REGISTER_FACTORY()` - With deprecated name support
   - `DECLARE_FACTORY()` - For linking static archives

4. **Factory Base Classes** (`envoy/config/typed_config.h`)
   - `UntypedFactory` - Base interface with `name()`, `category()`, `configTypes()`
   - `TypedFactory` - Adds protobuf configuration support

5. **Factory Lookup Utilities** (`source/common/config/utility.h`)
   - `Utility::getFactory()` - Lookup by name or type
   - `Utility::getFactoryByType()` - Type URL-based lookup
   - `Utility::getFactoryByName()` - Name-based lookup

### Self-Registration at Static Initialization

Extensions self-register through:
- Static global `RegisterFactory` instances (in static registration mode)
- Or `forceRegister*()` functions called during initialization
- Factory categories automatically registered on first factory r
... (truncated)

Envoy Extension Registry and Factory Architecture\\n\\nThe Envoy C++ codebase implements a sophisticated extension registry pattern for dynamic discovery and instantiation of extension implementations. This pattern is central to Envoy's plugin architecture.\\n\\n### Core Registry System\\n\\n**Registry Template Class (envoy/registry/registry.h:166)**\\n\\nThe `FactoryRegistry<Base>` template class is the core of the registry system. It maintains a static hash map of factory instances keyed by name using `factories()` (line 190), and provides factory lookup methods:\\n- `getFactory(name)` (line 293): Looks up factory by string name\\n- `getFactoryByType(type)` (line 302): Looks up factory by protobuf configuration type\\n- `registeredNames()` (line 171): Returns sorted vector of all registered factory names\\n- `registerFactory()` (line 230, 247): Registers factory instances with optional versioning\\n\\n**Factory Registration (envoy/registry/registry.h:507-597)**\\n\\nThe `RegisterFactory<T, Base>` template class is a CRTP-style registration mechanism. When instantiated (typically as a static variable), its constructor automatically registers a static instance of factory T with the FactoryRegistry<Base>. There are two variants:\\n\\n1. Static instantiation mode (ENVOY_STATIC_EXTENSION_REGISTRATION): Factories are registered via static global variables created by the REGISTER_FACTORY macro (line 622-626)\\n2. Dynamic registration mode: Factory registration is triggered via `forceRegister*()` functions (line 641-645) that create the RegisterFactory instances on-demand\\n\\n**Registration Macros (envoy/registry/registry.h:618-665)**\\n\\nThree key macros provide the public API:\\n\\n1. `REGISTER_FACTORY(FACTORY, BASE)` - Registers a factory class with a base class\\n2. `LEGACY_REGISTER_FACTORY(FACTORY, BASE, DEPRECATED_NAME)` - Registers with deprecated name support\\n3. `DECLARE_FACTORY(FACTORY)` - Declares the forceRegister function for linking in static archives\\n\\nThese macros expand to either static RegisterFactory instances or function definitions depending on the build configuration.\\n\\n### Factory Base Classes\\n\\n**Core Interfaces (envoy/config/typed_config.h)**\\n\\nAll factories derive from `UntypedFactory` (line 14), which defines the factory interface:\\n- `name()`: Returns the factory's name (reversed DNS recommended)\\n- `category()`: Returns the factory category for automatic registration\\n- `configTypes()`: Returns protobuf message types handled by the factory\\n\\nThe `TypedFactory` (line 41) subclass adds:\\n- `createEmptyConfigProto()`: Creates an empty configuration protobuf message\\n\\n**Filter Factory Hierarchies (envoy/server/filter_config.h)**\\n\\nThe filter config module defines specialized factory base classes:\\n- `ListenerFilterConfigFactoryBase`: Base for listener filters\\n- `NamedListenerFilterConfigFactory`: Listener filter factories\\n- `NamedUdpListenerFilterConfigFactory`: UDP listener filter factories  \\n- `NamedQuicListenerFilterConfigFactory`: QUIC listener filter factories\\n- `NamedNetworkFilterConfigFactory`: Downstream network filter factories\\n- `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory`: HTTP filter factories (line 273)\\n- `HttpFilterConfigFactoryBase`: Base class for HTTP filters\\n\\nEach defines a `category()` method returning the extension category (e.g., \\\"envoy.filters.http\\\").\\n\\n### Factory Lookup and Usage\\n\\n**Factory Lookup Utilities (source/common/config/utility.h)**\\n\\nThe `Utility` class (line 67) provides factory lookup methods:\\n\\n1. `getFactoryByName<Factory>(name)` (line 240): Looks up factory by name, returns nullptr if not found\\n2. `getFactory<Factory>(message)` (line 253): Looks up by type first, falls back to name if not found\\n3. `getFactoryByType<Factory>(typed_config)` (line 327): Looks up factory by protobuf configuration type URL\\n4. `getAndCheckFactory<Factory>(message)` (line 293): Lookup with error checking, throws if not found\\n\\nThese utilities internally call `Registry::FactoryRegistry<Factory>::getFactory()` and related methods.\\n\\n### Factory Category Registry\\n\\n**Category Registration (envoy/registry/registry.h:104-146)**\\n\\nThe `FactoryCategoryRegistry` maintains a map of factory categories. When a factory registers via RegisterFactory, it automatically registers its category if not already present (line 522-525). This enables:\\n- Discovering all available factory categories\\n- Querying factories by category\\n- Disabling factories by category name\\n\\n### Static Initialization and Self-Registration\\n\\n**Static Extension Registration Pattern**\\n\\nExtensions self-register at static initialization time through several mechanisms:\\n\\n1. **Global Variable Instantiation**: In static registration mode, each extension defines a static RegisterFactory instance. This is built by `buildFactoriesByType()` (line 355) which iterates through all registered factories and maps each configuration type returned by `factory->configTypes()` to the factory.\\n\\n**Factory Discovery by Configuration Type**\\n\\nWhen a configuration specifies a typed_config with a type URL, the lookup flow is:\\n1. Extract type URL from `envoy::config::core::v3::TypedExtensionConfig`\\n2. Call `getFactoryType()` to extract the message type name\\n3. Call `FactoryRegistry<Base>::getFactoryByType(type)`\\n4. Return the factory handling that configuration type\\n\\nThis enables configuration-driven extension discovery independent of factory names.\\n\\n### Test Infrastructure\\n\\n**InjectFactory Helper Class (test/test_common/registry.h:15-51)**\\n\\nFor testing, the `InjectFactory<Base>` class provides temporary factory registration:\\n- Constructor registers a factory instance\\n- Destructor automatically restores previous factory state\\n- Used instead of permanent REGISTER_FACTORY in most tests\\n\\n**InjectFactoryCategory** (line 54): Similar helper for temporary category registration.\\n\\n### Deprecated Factory Names\\n\\nThe registry supports deprecated factory names for backward compatibility (envoy/registry/registry.h:205-240):\\n- `deprecatedFactoryNames()` map tracks name aliases\\n- `registerFactory(factory, name, instead_value)` registers with deprecation mapping\\n- `canonicalFactoryName(name)` resolves deprecated names to canonical names\\n- Enables seamless migration when factory names change\\n\\n### Example Extension Registration Flow\\n\\nWhen source/extensions/filters/listener/original_dst/config.cc:60-61 executes:\\n```cpp\\nREGISTER_FACTORY(OriginalDstConfigFactory, \\n                 Server::Configuration::NamedListenerFilterConfigFactory){\\\"envoy.listener.original_dst\\\"};\\n```\\n\\nThis:\\n1.
